<div id="review_63563019" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/63563019" />
    <a title="Meaghan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/430758-meaghan"><img alt="Meaghan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1584945127p2/430758.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/63563019?book_show_action=true">Jul 15, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Meaghan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Meaghan" href="/user/show/430758-meaghan">Meaghan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/430758-meaghan?shelf=childrens-young-adult-fiction">childrens-young-adult-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/430758-meaghan?shelf=read-in-2009">read-in-2009</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer63563019" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12321693332861313982">People will be tempted to compare this book to Shelley Hrdlitschka's <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/3876163.Sister_Wife' title='Sister Wife by Shelley Hrdlitschka' rel='nofollow noopener'>Sister Wife</a>, which came out just months before The Chosen One. The books share certain similarities: both are about a girl in her early teens who lives in an insular polygamist community and yearns for life on the "outside." In both cases, the girl is in love with a boy her own age, but is commanded to marry an older man.<br/><br/>Williams's book, however, is much darker than Hrdlitschka's. I think the focus is also different. Hrdlitschk</span>
  <span id="freeText12321693332861313982" style="display:none">People will be tempted to compare this book to Shelley Hrdlitschka's <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/3876163.Sister_Wife" title="Sister Wife by Shelley Hrdlitschka" rel="nofollow noopener">Sister Wife</a>, which came out just months before The Chosen One. The books share certain similarities: both are about a girl in her early teens who lives in an insular polygamist community and yearns for life on the "outside." In both cases, the girl is in love with a boy her own age, but is commanded to marry an older man.<br /><br />Williams's book, however, is much darker than Hrdlitschka's. I think the focus is also different. Hrdlitschka tried very hard to present all sides of the polygamy issue and maintain a neutral point of view. In Williams's story, however, the male leaders of the community are indisputably evil, and one dark event follows another. An infant is deliberately ducked in water and nearly drowned simply because the previous day the adults were unable to stop her crying. Disabled babies are killed at birth. A teenage girl forced to marry a much older man is accused of adultery and murdered. And so on.<br /><br />Many people might accuse Williams of prejudice against polygamists, but the polygamy seemed almost incidental to the story. Take the polygamy out and you wouldn't lose much. You've still got girls into marriage with men many times their age, the murder of infants, etc. I think the story wasn't about polygamists, it was about an isolated and thoroughly cowed group of people in the grip of some truly terrible leaders. This book could have been about Jonestown. Or North Korea.<br /><br />The Chosen One is a quick read. Not only is it relatively short at a little over 200 pages, but the atmosphere of suspense -- as the protagonist's wedding date approaches -- kept me rapidly turning pages. I actually found it more realistic than Sister Wife, particularly at the end. The ending is ambiguous and it's clear that the girl and her family's troubles are far from over, but it was about as hopeful as you could reasonably expect.<br /><br />I liked the story a lot, but it's not for everyone. The sheer darkness of it, and the violence, make it lean towards the older end of the YA spectrum, though the protagonist is only thirteen.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12321693332861313982" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_53868323" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/53868323" />
    <a title="Kristi" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1310688-kristi"><img alt="Kristi" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1496094866p2/1310688.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/53868323?book_show_action=true">Apr 24, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kristi" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kristi" href="/user/show/1310688-kristi">Kristi</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer53868323" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5113191488612801274">This novel was nothing short of spectacular. This is a very intense topic and I was glad to see it represented in a young adult novel. I was enraged, disgusted, and saddened by this novel. <br/><br/>Told from Kyra’s point of view, this novel unfolds a story of desperation, love, fear, and freedom. Kyra’s internal struggle was masterfully depicted. I never once questioned her desire to stay. Why would you not? To leave your family and everything you have come to know. I only hope that I would posses that t</span>
  <span id="freeText5113191488612801274" style="display:none">This novel was nothing short of spectacular. This is a very intense topic and I was glad to see it represented in a young adult novel. I was enraged, disgusted, and saddened by this novel. <br /><br />Told from Kyra’s point of view, this novel unfolds a story of desperation, love, fear, and freedom. Kyra’s internal struggle was masterfully depicted. I never once questioned her desire to stay. Why would you not? To leave your family and everything you have come to know. I only hope that I would posses that type of courage, that she must have had to posses in order to leave. <br /><br />Williams seamlessly balanced Kyra’s world. At one end of the spectrum Kyra’s family is full of love, from her father and her many mothers, sharing many of the same qualities, you’d expect from any family, polygamous or not. And yet the other end contains the darker side, the killing of defective babies, beating, and tortuous discipline. It’s almost impossible not to become emotionally invested in this story. <br /><br />There was one aspect that bothered me, and it had to do with the cell phone. And perhaps it was just me, but for as completely forbidden everything from the outside world was, I find it very hard to believe that Kyra could operate a cell phone with such ease. But despite that small complaint, I don’t feel that it took away from the story. <br /><br />Overall, all the hype had it right: <br />“Compelling”<br />“powerful”<br />“a masterpiece”<br />“an important book”<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="5113191488612801274" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_48919922" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/48919922" />
    <a title="Jessica" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/202724-jessica"><img alt="Jessica" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1601676054p2/202724.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/48919922?book_show_action=true">Mar 11, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jessica" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jessica" href="/user/show/202724-jessica">Jessica</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/202724-jessica?shelf=youngadult">youngadult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer48919922" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1387255743865455733">A heart-breaking work of great beauty. Williams delves into the conflicted heart of a young girl, raised in a strict polygamous sect, who is trying to break free. She is bound to marry her 60-year-old uncle in a matter of weeks, something that she would rather die than do. But if she defies the church, what will the consequences be for her family? And if she leaves it all behind, will she ever see anyone she loves again?<br/><br/>Gripping from the first page, beautifully written, piercing.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1852938754" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1852938754" />
    <a title="Katherine" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/13311251-katherine"><img alt="Katherine" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577842427p2/13311251.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1852938754?book_show_action=true">Feb 19, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Katherine" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Katherine" href="/user/show/13311251-katherine">Katherine</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780312627751" href="/book/show/7919992-the-chosen-one">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13311251-katherine?shelf=instalove-express">instalove-express</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13311251-katherine?shelf=kick-ass-mc">kick-ass-mc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13311251-katherine?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13311251-katherine?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13311251-katherine?shelf=fast-paced">fast-paced</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13311251-katherine?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13311251-katherine?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13311251-katherine?shelf=cults">cults</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1852938754" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8579065693145034518"><b>
  <i>”’We’re safe here,’ Father had said. ‘We’re away from everyone. Alone. Safe. Out here. Just us. Just The Chosen Ones.'”</i>
</b><br/><br/>What would you do if you couldn’t choose? Choose who you want to marry, or how many spouses your husband marries? How many children you want? What you can read, watch, and do? We seem to take it all for granted, and in this harrowing read, Carol Lynch Williams takes us into the world of Kyra Leigh Carlson, <b>who has the ability to choose none of the above.</b><br/><br/>Thirteen-year-old Kyr</span>
  <span id="freeText8579065693145034518" style="display:none"><b>
  <i>”’We’re safe here,’ Father had said. ‘We’re away from everyone. Alone. Safe. Out here. Just us. Just The Chosen Ones.'”</i>
</b><br /><br />What would you do if you couldn’t choose? Choose who you want to marry, or how many spouses your husband marries? How many children you want? What you can read, watch, and do? We seem to take it all for granted, and in this harrowing read, Carol Lynch Williams takes us into the world of Kyra Leigh Carlson, <b>who has the ability to choose none of the above.</b><br /><br />Thirteen-year-old Kyra Leigh lives with her twenty brothers and sisters, three mothers, and father in isolation in the Utah desert under the watchful eye of the Prophet. They are part of the Chosen Ones (a very polite way of saying a sect of the FLDS). She’s expected to be a dutiful daughter and someday a dutiful wife. But she’s never felt comfortable in the strict confines of her overbearing way of existence. The temptation to disobey and want more is too much to take.<blockquote>
  <i>”’Looking outside the fence, going outside the fence alone is dangerous,’ Mother said. ‘It’s like standing too close to the edge of a cliff. You peer over the side, you might fall. You might lose what you have.’<br /><br />But I looked anyway.”</i>
</blockquote>Stifled by her lack of freedom to choose, she begins small acts of rebellion, such as her checking out forbidden books from the mobile library and her relationship with a boy whom she has chosen for herself.<blockquote>
  <i>”My sins.<br />A plan. Books. And a boy.<br />There’s a boy.”</i>
</blockquote>But when Prophet Childs has a vision that she is to marry her 60-year-old uncle, Kyra must find a way to escape, or be doomed to live a life of servitude to a man she does not love and in a life she never wanted.<br /><br /><b>I’ve always had a strange fascination with cults.</b> I can’t really explain it though. But with all the stories that have been in the media about different (albeit horrible) incidents involving cults, it only stirs the pot to a particularly fascinating subject matter. The author takes us inside what it might be like to live in a place and in a religion like that. How the people get so brainwashed that they’ll believe just about anything. How so little freedom they have compared to us that it might as well be that they live in a third world country. No rights to their bodies, no right to their ideas, no right to say or do what they please. <b>No right to even utter the word ‘no’.</b> And I have absolutely no idea if some of the plot points in the book actually take place inside the FLDS commune, but if they do, it’s doubly horrifying.<br /><br />The authors writes in such a way that you feel like you’re actually there. There were some parts of the book where I could feel myself breaking out into a sweat, and my heart start to race because the writing was so raw and visceral. And Kyra was such a likable and believable character that <b>you can’t help but root for her</b>. Even when she’s literally coming up with an assassination plot to kill the prophet, cause I mean lets face it; you kind of want her to actually go along with it because he’s such a horrible person.<blockquote>
  <i>”’If I was going to kill the Prophet,’ I say, not even keeping my voice low, ‘I’d do it in Africa.’<br /><br />I’m sure I’m the only Chosen One who has wished the Prophet dead and his body picked away by termites.”</i>
</blockquote>I could have done without all the bemoaning about her sweetheart Joshua, but then I reminded myself that 1)She’s barely fourteen, most of them think like that; and 2)Let her do it. It’s really the only thing she has control over. Stop being a curmudgeonly grandma.<br /><br />I also was a bit confused at the interspersing of verse sections in this novel. I’ve never been a fan of novels in verse, and <b>it honestly felt out of place in this book.</b> They were interspersed randomly throughout and with little thought or motive. It’s as if the author tried to do it to spice things up, but just made it confusing in the process.<br /><br />The Chosen One is a harrowing, haunting read with a main character that will stay with you long after the final page has turned, and will have you counting your blessings that <b>you have the simple, blessed freedom to choose.</b><blockquote>
  <i>”’Kyra,’ he said, ‘you must be obedient. You must do as the you’re told. Stay home. Stay close.’<br /><br />‘What’s out there?’<br /><br />Father was silent. <br /><br />Then he said, ‘<b>The world.</b>’”</i>
</blockquote></span>
  <a data-text-id="8579065693145034518" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText836118437481929142" style="display:none">Well upon reading the summary, I was intrigued.<br />I like learning about polygamist communities because they're so unique... and frightening. <br />However, this book started off promising, but by the end I was puzzled and very annoyed.<br />Here we have the main character Kyra, a kind and interesting main character who falls in love with someone she shouldn't love. We meet her family and siblings who are all charming.<br /><br />Then we meet the enemy, the Prophet who insists that Kyra marries her cruel uncle who already has a bunch of other wives.<br /><br />As always, I try not spoil much, but I will say this:<br />The majority of the novel was truthful. From the young, naïve love to the struggle of keeping your faith and family together. But it fell flat at the end. <br />At the end (spoilers, do not read!!!) when she was trying to escape with Patrick and he was killed, I felt like that part was glossed over when it could've had a big impact. She received no punishment for it either, not that I wanted her to be punished, but considering every that happened previously...<br />Second, when she finally did escape, it was not as thrilling as I hoped. She was brought to some house, spoke to some lady, and it was over. No resolution. What happened to her family? The boy she loved? Patrick's family? There was nothing!<br />In the end, the novel wasn't horrible, but disappointing.</span>

<div id="review_417884049" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/417884049" />
    <a title="Cassi aka Snow White Haggard" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2216677-cassi-aka-snow-white-haggard"><img alt="Cassi aka Snow White Haggard" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1321462468p2/2216677.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/417884049?book_show_action=true">Sep 19, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cassi aka Snow White Haggard" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cassi aka Snow White Haggard" href="/user/show/2216677-cassi-aka-snow-white-haggard">Cassi aka Snow White Haggard</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2216677-cassi-aka-snow-white-haggard?shelf=audio-books">audio-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2216677-cassi-aka-snow-white-haggard?shelf=read-in-2012">read-in-2012</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer417884049" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4548056732910549656">The Chosen One is one of those stories that is heart-wrenching and feels like it could be a true story. It's not. However, Kyra's voice is so authentic and she carries this novel. She's youthful yet wise, but not in a way that feels like an adult interjecting themselves into a child protagonist For Kyra, growing up in polygamist compound she's had to grow up fast. At thirteen, she's spent most of her life raising her younger siblings and being given adult responsibilities.<br/><br/>Even though her father </span>
  <span id="freeText4548056732910549656" style="display:none">The Chosen One is one of those stories that is heart-wrenching and feels like it could be a true story. It's not. However, Kyra's voice is so authentic and she carries this novel. She's youthful yet wise, but not in a way that feels like an adult interjecting themselves into a child protagonist For Kyra, growing up in polygamist compound she's had to grow up fast. At thirteen, she's spent most of her life raising her younger siblings and being given adult responsibilities.<br /><br />Even though her father is a good man and tries to protect Kyra, she's seen enough to understand the world around her. She's seen the young women married to old men, seen the women who fight-back ostracized. Yet Kyra is still hopeful. That's part of what makes Kyra both tragic and realistic. Like any child, she dreams of her own potential happiness. She wants to have a choice in life, to marry her crush Joshua, not to be a child-bride to an older man. She really believes that she might have a chance.<br /><br />That is until the prophet has a "vision" of Kyra's and sees her marry her own uncle, an elder in the compound who already has six wives.<br /><br />This story shines because it doesn't pretend there is an easy answer for Kyra. She's thirteen and faced with an unwanted marriage, or potentially running away and leaving the family she loves. On the outside it's easy to say Kyra should run. But Kyra struggles are more realistic. She loves her father, her mother and her gaggle of siblings. Just a child herself she can't imagine life outside the home she's always known.<br /><br />This book navigates that inner conflict and the choices Kyra must make beautifully, without oversimplifying the problem. The Chosen tackles a difficult issue with rare respect and intelligence.<br /><br />This audiobook is narrated by the wonderful Jenna Lamia, who captures the story perfectly. For a thoughtful and genuine book this is highly recommended.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4548056732910549656" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer1510450447" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer14611624197968026121">I said recently that the word 'cult' is a real buzz word for me, I am always excited to pick up books surrounding this topic and yet somehow I always ends up disappointed by them and, unfortunately, that was the case again here.<br/><br/>I, as always with these stories, loved the premise but found the execution to be somewhat lacking. The story was enjoyable but I found the writing to be very fragmented and the story kind of hard to connect with. <a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[<br/><br/>I really struggled with the scene that invol</span></span>
  <span id="freeText14611624197968026121" style="display:none">I said recently that the word 'cult' is a real buzz word for me, I am always excited to pick up books surrounding this topic and yet somehow I always ends up disappointed by them and, unfortunately, that was the case again here.<br /><br />I, as always with these stories, loved the premise but found the execution to be somewhat lacking. The story was enjoyable but I found the writing to be very fragmented and the story kind of hard to connect with. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[<br /><br />I really struggled with the scene that involved the depiction of punishing a baby of less than a year of age by holding it under water but, unfortunately, I know that things like these do go on in some communities as disgusting as it is.<br /><br />I also found the scene with the murder of the mobile-library driver to be a little hard to believe. How do these cult members expect to get away with murdering someone outside of their own organisation? That just didn't make a whole lot of sense to me.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />I also wish that the story would have provided a little more closure at the end.<br /><br />Overall I did enjoy the story and I will continue to picking up books in this genre hoping that one will eventually completely blow me away.</span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1658094929" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer468868561754818523"> The Chosen One offers an insightful look into a religious cult and the realistic hold that it has on its people. Carol Lynch Williams suggests sexual abuse through forced marriage, but deals primarily with the physical abuse and the heavy emotional captivity.<br/> I love the main character, Kyra. She is strongly determined, caring, and bookish. <br/> The Chosen One reminded me of Keep Sweet by Michelle Greene, perhaps more than any other book has ever reminded me of another. I imagine that there are cert</span>
  <span id="freeText468868561754818523" style="display:none"> The Chosen One offers an insightful look into a religious cult and the realistic hold that it has on its people. Carol Lynch Williams suggests sexual abuse through forced marriage, but deals primarily with the physical abuse and the heavy emotional captivity.<br /> I love the main character, Kyra. She is strongly determined, caring, and bookish. <br /> The Chosen One reminded me of Keep Sweet by Michelle Greene, perhaps more than any other book has ever reminded me of another. I imagine that there are certain hallmarks of these cults that would make one similar to the other.<br /> I think that it is important to remember that while The Chosen is written as fiction, these sort of religious cults are real and active today. These woman are often put in a positions where they have to choose whether to stay, or to leave their own children or siblings behind in order to save themselves. It is a horrific form of abuse. These girls are groomed their entire lives, and taught that it is all God ordained.</span>
  <a data-text-id="468868561754818523" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1360821545?book_show_action=true">Mar 31, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Brooke" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Brooke" href="/user/show/16610521-brooke">Brooke</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780312627751" href="/book/show/7919992-the-chosen-one">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16610521-brooke?shelf=owned-books">owned-books</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1360821545" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5517365561949502423">Kyra has grown up in an isolated, polygamist cult where the Prophet has total control over everyone and everything. She is just 13-years-old when the Prophet decrees that she must marry her 60-year-old uncle, which causes her to question everything she has been taught.<br/><br/>I am a sucker for books about cults, and I read <i>The Chosen One</i> in one sitting. The author did a good job of shaping the world and writing believable characters, especially given how short this book is. There were a few things that </span>
  <span id="freeText5517365561949502423" style="display:none">Kyra has grown up in an isolated, polygamist cult where the Prophet has total control over everyone and everything. She is just 13-years-old when the Prophet decrees that she must marry her 60-year-old uncle, which causes her to question everything she has been taught.<br /><br />I am a sucker for books about cults, and I read <i>The Chosen One</i> in one sitting. The author did a good job of shaping the world and writing believable characters, especially given how short this book is. There were a few things that felt off to me (such as the fact that Kyra was able to use a cellphone with ease, despite having never seen one before) and the ending left me with several unanswered questions. Overall, it wasn’t the best fictionalized cult book that I’ve ever read, but it wasn’t the worst. It was a quick read, which would likely be better received by those just starting to fall down the rabbit hole of cult-related stories. </span>
  <a data-text-id="5517365561949502423" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('y8gN582VuVghGzEgfehXQzlRCGrGXhBTN6VWqCgUCiXCTH1jsnow7AABDPoUpsGYgcH6DLXCP1Dcv9CDsTmGmg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('KgknGGtIc+2QRezLCVINwKlrlZGRB2N23UsDu1qtwLMjjVecFKf6WbFf0RFgHJsbEftn9+KbTHU2UYWQw4BMDA==')})
  }

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/288481.Carol_Lynch_Williams">About Carol Lynch Williams</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/288481.Carol_Lynch_Williams"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1332263501p3/288481.jpg);'></div>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer17338026941821128042">Carol Lynch Williams is the author of more than 30 books for middle grade and young adult readers. Her novels include The Chosen One, Never that Far, Messenger and Never Said. Her most recent book is the novelization of the movie Once I Was a Beehive. Carol has an MFA from Vermont College in Writing for Children and Young Adults and teaches creative writing at BYU. She runs Writing and Illustratin</span>
  <span id="freeText17338026941821128042" style="display:none">Carol Lynch Williams is the author of more than 30 books for middle grade and young adult readers. Her novels include The Chosen One, Never that Far, Messenger and Never Said. Her most recent book is the novelization of the movie Once I Was a Beehive. Carol has an MFA from Vermont College in Writing for Children and Young Adults and teaches creative writing at BYU. She runs Writing and Illustrating for Young Readers, a week-long writing conference for the not-faint-of-heart writer (<a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.wifyr.com">www.wifyr.com</a>). As well she is a mentor for those who want to write for kids and teens. Her best creative effort, however, are her five daughters. </span>
  <a data-text-id="17338026941821128042" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>
